[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 28-05-2026
in WP No. 5367/2026 passed by the High Court of Judicature at

KALE PRAVIN GANPAT & ORS.                          PETITIONER(S)

IA No. 178681/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 29-06-2026 These matters were called for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE R. MAHADEVAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ALOK ARADHE
     (PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) :
SLP(C) 21647/2026  Ms. Meenakshi Arora, Sr. Adv.

1

--- Page 18 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21647/2026
                   Ms. Gayathri, AOR
                   Mr. Jarnail Singh, Adv.          
SLP(C) 21665/2026  Mr. Amol Karande, Adv.
                   Mr. Kiran Magar, Adv.
                   Mr. B Lakhsmi Pallesh, Adv.
                   Mr. Ashutosh Srivastava, Adv.
                   Ms. Gayathri, AOR
                   Mr. Jarnail Singh, Adv.                         
For Respondent(s) : 
R.No.1 in          Mr. Sudhanshu S. Choudhari, Sr. Adv. (Through VC)
SLP(C) 21647/2026
R.Nos. 4 to 12 in  Mr. Sravan Kumar Karanam, AOR
SLP(C) 21647/2026  Mr. Santosh Kumar Yadav, Adv.
          UPON hearing the counsel, the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
Heard learned counsel for the parties.
2. The  learned  senior  counsel  appearing  for  the
petitioners submits that the dispute pertains to the
eligibility of 22 individual shareholder-members to be
included in the voters’ list for the election to the Board
of  Directors  of  the  Aurangabad  District  Central
Co-operative Bank Ltd. for the tenure 2026-2031. It is
contended that Resolution No. 20 approving the induction
as members, the issuance of share certificates dated
29.02.2024, the deposit of the requisite share/admission
amount on 14.03.2024, and their participation in the
Annual General Meeting held on 29.09.2025 establish that
2

--- Page 19 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21647/2026
their membership stood completed before the relevant cut-
off date. It is further submitted that the objections
raised by respondent no. 1 were politically motivated and
that respondent no. 1 had no locus standi to challenge the
petitioners’ membership.
3. Per  contra,  learned  senior  counsel  appearing  for
respondent no. 1 submits that in terms of Section 27(3A)
of the Maharashtra Co-operative Societies Act, 1960, an
individual member becomes entitled to vote only upon
completion of two years from the date of enrolment and
therefore,  the  members  concerned  ought  to  have  been
enrolled on or before 21.03.2024. It is submitted that the
petitioners had not completed the statutory period of two
years as on the qualifying date and were therefore rightly
excluded from the voters’ list. It is further contended
that the Bank’s Annual Report reflected only 59 individual
members as on 31.03.2024, whereas the draft voters’ list
contained 80 names; that the requisite share / admission
amounts  had  not  been  deposited  along  with  the
applications; and that the membership registers in Forms
‘I’ and ‘J’ recorded the date of admission / payment as
12.04.2024. Learned senior counsel also contends that the
counterfoils of the challans relied upon to establish
remittance of the requisite fee are not genuine. It is
3

--- Page 20 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21647/2026
therefore,  submitted  that  the  objections  filed  by
respondent no. 1 were rightly accepted by the Election
Officer, which order has been affirmed by the High Court.
While seeking time to file a counter affidavit, learned
senior counsel further submits that the election process
has already commenced and any interim order in favour of
the petitioners would disrupt the election schedule.  
4. Having regard to the rival submissions, the issue as
the date of completion of the petitioners’ membership and
the deposit of the requisite admission / share amount
involves  disputed  questions  of  fact,  which  require
consideration on the basis of the material to be placed
before this court. In the meantime, it is directed that
the election process shall proceed as scheduled. However,
the result of the election shall remain subject to the
outcome of these Special Leave Petitions.
5. List the matters after four weeks. 
6. Respondent No. 1 shall file his counter affidavit, by
then.
  (POOJA SHARMA)                                  (AVGV RAMU)
     AR-CUM-PS                                 COURT MASTER (NSH)
4

--- Page 21 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21647/2026

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
INHERENT JURISDICTION
CONTEMPT PETITION (C) No. 981/2019 
in 
WRIT PETITION (C) No. 1001/2017
MOHAMMAD WAQAS KHAN & ORS.             PETITIONER(s)
                                VERSUS
DR. HEMANT GADEKAR & ANR.                       RESPONDENT(s)
 O R D E R
Present Contempt Petition has been filed by Petitioners
who are MBBS students alleging wilful disobedience of the
order/judgment dated 17 th January 2019 passed by this Court in
Writ Petition (C) No. 1001 of 2017.  The relevant portion of
the said direction is reproduced hereinbelow:-
“18.  ……
(iv) The students are entitled to receive the
refund of fee paid by them for admission to the
College for the academic year 2017-19.  In addition,
the College is directed to pay a compensation of Rs.
One Lakh to the said students.”
2. On the last date of hearing i.e. 22 nd November 2019,
learned counsel for Respondent had stated that the aforesaid
order dated 17 th January 2019 has been complied with.  On the
said date of hearing, learned counsel for students had taken
time  to  verify  the  said  fact.  Thereafter,  neither  any
application nor any affidavit has been placed on record by the
students. Today also, none is present for the petitioners.
1

--- Page 30 ---
3. Accordingly, present Contempt Petition is disposed of as
satisfied.
4. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.
………………………………………………………J.
                                          ( MANMOHAN )       
 
…………………………………………………………J.
                                       ( K. VINOD CHANDRAN )  
NEW DELHI; 
JUNE 30, 2026
2

--- Page 31 ---

                             O R D E R
Applications for exemption from filing certified copy of
the impugned judgment is allowed.   
We have heard the learned Senior counsel appearing for
the petitioners and the learned Senior counsel appearing for the
respondent.
Issue notice.
Learned counsel appearing for the respondent on caveat,
accepts notice. 
Though,  this  Special  Leave  Petition  is  against  the

--- Page 33 ---
2
dismissal of the writ petition, it is submitted by the learned
Senior counsel appearing for the petitioners that if the directions
in the impugned order are given effect to, nothing would survive in
the pending suit. However, the learned Senior counsel appearing for
the respondent submitted that in view of the specific finding on
the facts given by the Courts below, there is no need to interfere
with the impugned order. 
Considering the submissions made at the bar, at this
stage,  we  permit  the  respondent  to  withdraw  the  amount  of
Rs.2,50,00,000/- (Rupees Two Crores and Fifty Lakhs) deposited
before the Registry of the High Court.
The petitioner shall also make payment of a further
amount of Rs.1,00,00,000/- (Rupees One Crore) to the respondent,
without prejudice to the contentions raised in the Special Leave
Petition, within a period of four weeks from the date of receipt of
a copy of this order.  
That  leaves  us  to  the  remaining  amount  ordered.
Considering the nature of dispute, we expect the parties to resolve
the matter between themselves with the able assistance of the
learned Senior counsel appearing for them. 
In view of the above, the 22 bank accounts of the
petitioners which have been frozen ought to be de-freezed, so as to
enable the petitioners to run their other institutions. The same
would be subject to the payment of the aforesaid amount of
Rs.1,00,00,000/- by the petitioners to the respondent
List the matter on 12.08.2026.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL ORIGINAL JURISDICTION
TRANSFER PETITION(S)(CIVIL) NO.   563/2026  
GULBAKHOR                                         Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
FAREED KHAN                                       Respondent(s)
O R D E R
1. This petition has been filed by the petitioner-wife seeking
transfer of Petition bearing No. 546 of 2025, titled as "Fareed
Khan vs. Gulabkhor ”, pending before the Principal Judge, Family
Courts, Alwar, Rajasthan to the Principal Judge, Family Courts,
South-East District, Saket Courts, Delhi. 
2. Despite being duly served with the notice, none is present for
the respondent. Hence, it appears that the respondent has no
objection if the present petition is transferred, as prayed for.
3. Heaving heard learned counsel for the petitioner,  we are
inclined to transfer the case sought for. We, accordingly, allow
the transfer petition and direct that Petition bearing No.546 of
2025, titled as  "Fareed Khan vs. Gulabkhor ”, pending before the
Principal Judge, Family Courts, Alwar, Rajasthan be transferred to
the Principal Judge, Family Courts, South-East District, Saket
Courts, Delhi. 
4. However, if the video conferencing facility is available with
1

--- Page 39 ---
the Court, the benefit of the same shall be extended to the
parties, unless their physical presence is required.
5. The transferor Court shall forthwith transmit the record of
the aforesaid case to the transferee court.
6. The transferee Court shall make all possible endeavours first
for an amicable settlement between the parties, failing which for
early decision in the matter without unnecessary adjournments.
7. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of. 
  
  ……………………………………………………………………J.
                        [K.V. VISWANATHAN]
       ………………………………………………………………………J.
    [SHREE CHANDRASHEKHAR]
NEW DELHI;

                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition(s) for Special Leave to Appeal (Crl.) No(s). 7184/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  16-02-2026
in SBCRMBA No. 16120/2025 passed by the High Court of Judicature
for Rajasthan at Jaipur]
MOHAMMAD WASIM                                     Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
STATE OF RAJASTHAN & ANR.                          Respondent(s)
Mr. Amit Pai, Ld. AOR has been appointed as Amicus Curiae vide
Court's order dated 29.06.2026 
 
Date : 01-07-2026 This petition was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE K.V. VISWANATHAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE SHREE CHANDRASHEKHAR
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) : Mr. Abhisar Bhanu , AOR
                   
For Respondent(s) :Ms. Sansriti Pathak, A.A.G.
                   Mr. Saurabh Rajpal, AOR
    Ms. Shagufa Khan, Adv.
                   
                   Mr. Amit Pai, AOR
                   Ms. Bhavana Duhoon, Adv.
                   Mr. Siddharth S. Chapalgaonkar, Adv.
                   
                   
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Heard Mr. Abhisar Bhanu, learned counsel for the
petitioner,  Ms.  Sansriti  Pathak,  learned  Additional
Solicitor General, appearing for the State and Mr. Amit
1

--- Page 42 ---
Pai, learned Amicus Curiae, appearing for the de-facto
complainant.
2. This petitioner calls in question the correctness
of  the  order  dated  16.02.2026  in  S.B.  Criminal
Miscellaneous Bail Application No. 16120/2025, passed by
the High Court of Judicature at Rajasthan at Jaipur. By
the said said order, the petitioner has been denied the
benefit of bail in connection with FIR No.345/2025,
registered at Police Station – Jaisinghpura Khor, Jaipur
North, for the offences punishable under Sections 64(1)
of the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023 (for short, ‘BNS’)
and 3 and 4 of the Protection of Children from Sexual
Offences Act, 2012 (for short, ‘POCSO’). 
3. Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that
the petitioner had already undergone eight months in
custody. Learned counsel also draws attention to the
deposition  of  PW-1  (prosecutrix)  and  submits  that
admittedly, the prosecutrix refused to undergo medical
examination. He also draws attention to that portion of
the statement, where the prosecutrix admitted that the
room, in which the incident is alleged to have happened,
was taken by her, and not provided by the accused.
Learned counsel for the petitioner also submits that
earlier, there was a similar case instituted against
one,  Jamir  Afridi,  which  resulted  in  an  acquittal
2

--- Page 43 ---
because the prosecutrix recanted from her statement. He
further submits that the trial is bound to take some
time, since five witnesses remained to be examined.
4. Learned counsel for the State and learned Amicus
Curiae, defend the impugned order.
5. Having  considered  the  overall  facts  and
circumstances of the case and considering the period
undergone, we are inclined to enlarge the petitioner on
bail.
6. Accordingly, we direct that the petitioner be
enlarged on bail subject to the satisfaction of the
Trial  Court,  in  connection  with  Sessions  Case  No.
02/2025,  pending  on  the  court  of  Special  Judge
Protection of Children from Sexual Offences Act 2012,
Serial No. 01, Jaipur Metropolitan, II.
7. We place on record our appreciation to Mr. Amit
Pai,  learned  Amicus  Curiae  who  ably  prepared  and
presented the case. 
8. The Special Leave Petition is disposed of in the
above terms.
9. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand
disposed of.
  (RAHUL KUMAR)                                  (MANOJ KUMAR)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)

possession, list the matters on 03.07.2026.

deferred until the next date of hearing i.e. 03.07.2026.
We make it clear that the appeals themselves shall be
disposed of on 03.07.2026.

1

--- Page 101 ---
withdrawal of 50% of the amount shall be allowed only

nationalized  bank  for  the  said  amount  to  the

made clear that it shall be kept in a fixed deposit so
that it earns a maximum interest. The same may be kept
in a nationalized bank.

the these matters can be disposed of to enable the
High Court to hear and decide the matter finally. We
order accordingly.

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Having heard Mr. Tushar Mehta, learned Solicitor General
for India, Mr. Parag P. Tripathi, learned Senior Counsel
appearing  on  caveat  for  respondent  no.2  supporting  the
petitioner and Mr. Gaurav Chopra, learned Senior Counsel
appearing on caveat for the respondent no.1, we find no good
ground to interfere with the impugned judgment/order.
2. At  this  stage,  Mr.  Tushar  Mehta,  learned  Solicitor
General for India drawing attention to paragraph 76 of the
impugned order, submits that the direction should not be
construed to be coming in the way of the petitioner exercising
any other right under the notice inviting tender.
3. Needless to add that the impugned order has only dealt
with the rejection of the first respondent’s bid as Non-
Responsive. If there are any other rights vested in the
petitioner under the tender conditions, they would absolutely
not be affected.
4. With these observations, the Special Leave Petition is
disposed of.
5. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand disposed
of.
